    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16153257860662900684">Stephen King returns to the rich landscape of Mid-World, the spectacular territory of the Dark Tower fantasy saga that stands as his most beguiling achievement. <br/><br/>Roland Deschain and his ka-tet<i>—</i>Jake, Susannah, Eddie, and Oy, the billy-bumbler—encounter a ferocious storm just after crossing the River Whye on their way to the Outer Baronies. As they shelter from the howling ga</span>
  <span id="freeText16153257860662900684" style="display:none">Stephen King returns to the rich landscape of Mid-World, the spectacular territory of the Dark Tower fantasy saga that stands as his most beguiling achievement. <br /><br />Roland Deschain and his ka-tet<i>—</i>Jake, Susannah, Eddie, and Oy, the billy-bumbler—encounter a ferocious storm just after crossing the River Whye on their way to the Outer Baronies. As they shelter from the howling gale, Roland tells his friends not just one strange story but two . . . and in so doing, casts new light on his own troubled past. <br /><br />In his early days as a gunslinger, in the guilt-ridden year following his mother’s death, Roland is sent by his father to investigate evidence of a murderous shape-shifter, a “skin-man” preying upon the population around Debaria. Roland takes charge of Bill Streeter, the brave but terrified boy who is the sole surviving witness to the beast’s most recent slaughter. Only a teenager himself, Roland calms the boy and prepares him for the following day’s trials by reciting a story from the <i>Magic Tales of the Eld </i>that his mother often read to him at bedtime. “A person’s never too old for stories,” Roland says to Bill. “Man and boy, girl and woman, never too old. We live for them.” And indeed, the tale that Roland unfolds, the legend of Tim Stoutheart, is a timeless treasure for all ages, a story that lives for us.<br /><br />King began the Dark Tower series in 1974; it gained momentum in the 1980s; and he brought it to a thrilling conclusion when the last three novels were published in 2003 and 2004. <i>The Wind Through the Keyhole </i>is sure to fascinate avid fans of the Dark Tower epic. But this novel also stands on its own for all readers, an enchanting and haunting journey to Roland’s world and testimony to the power of Stephen King’s storytelling magic.<br /><br />~from first edition jacket</span>
  <a data-text-id="16153257860662900684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

    <div id=buyButtonContainer class="uitext buttons buyableFeature u-marginTopXSmall u-paddingBottomXSmall u-bottomGrayBorder" data-book-id=12341557 >

    <div class="u-positionRelative">

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/310419-i-have-read-the-entire-dark-tower-series">I have read the entire Dark Tower series except for The Wind Through the Keyhole. I know it&#39;s a connection between books 4 and 5, and mostly a flashback of Roland&#39;s younger years, but I&#39;d like to know if the people who have read it would recommend reading it between those books, or reading it after book 7. Which way flows better?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_310419'><a id="like_count_community_question_310419" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/310419?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">8 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F12341557-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/310419-i-have-read-the-entire-dark-tower-series">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>

</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/22223794-eileen"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1419433822i/22223794._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/22223794-eileen">Eileen</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I read it after the core DT series, after a few months. I highly recommend the same as it provides a bit of nostalgia value. I think reading it betwee<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I read it after the core DT series, after a few months. I highly recommend the same as it provides a bit of nostalgia value. I think reading it between books 4 and 5 will chop up the story a bit too much -- a lot of action happens during that time and you don't want to get derailed.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/464920-i-accidently-bought-this-book-first">I accidently bought this book FIRST! :/ should I just read it or do I need to read the others first?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_464920'><a id="like_count_community_question_464920" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/464920?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F12341557-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/464920-i-accidently-bought-this-book-first">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/464920-i-accidently-bought-this-book-first">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/17145578-nick-lugo"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1376014198i/17145578._UX100_CR0,2,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/17145578-nick-lugo">Nick Lugo</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">My suggestion is absolutely stick with the original order and then read this between Wizard and Glass and Wolves of the Calla. It starts up just after<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">My suggestion is absolutely stick with the original order and then read this between Wizard and Glass and Wolves of the Calla. It starts up just after Glass and ruins parts of both The Waste Land and Wizard and Glass (major enough parts that i would avoid this at all costs)<br /><br />My suggestion for my friends has been read 1-4, then Wind, then 5-7, then read the graphic novels and the short story Little Sisters of Eluria. You could read the first few Graphic Novels after Wizard and before Calla, because the first (5 I think) couple are really all about Roland's past.<br /><br />Also, if you wanna get crazy with it, you should read Insomnia, Salem's Lot, The Stand, The Talisman, Black House, Eye of the Dragon, Hearts in Atlantis, Rose Madder, and From a Buick 8- all of which have some bearing on the quest for the tower.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_307664649" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/307664649" />
    <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence"><img alt="Mark Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307664649?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Lawrence" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307664649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12719161554679474433">The headline here is that I almost never read a book in 3 days - but I did this one and I was up past my bedtime turning pages.<br/><br/>Stephen King has written this series across the whole span of his adult life & both the character and quality of the series change across the decades (and also between front and back cover). For me Dark Tower as a whole is often spectacular, sometimes a bit weak, but mostly very good. <br/><br/>The Wind Through The Keyhole (TWTTK) is set just after my favourite of the series 'Wiza</span>
  <span id="freeText12719161554679474433" style="display:none">The headline here is that I almost never read a book in 3 days - but I did this one and I was up past my bedtime turning pages.<br /><br />Stephen King has written this series across the whole span of his adult life &amp; both the character and quality of the series change across the decades (and also between front and back cover). For me Dark Tower as a whole is often spectacular, sometimes a bit weak, but mostly very good. <br /><br />The Wind Through The Keyhole (TWTTK) is set just after my favourite of the series 'Wizard and Glass' and focuses on the Gilead days (my favourite part of Wizard and Glass) so there was always going to be a good chance I'd like it.<br /><br />This is a story within a story within a story, and most of the book is spent at the deepest layer of this Russian doll. King is returning to ground he last trod 15 years ago and it's as if he never left.<br /><br />There's nothing in TWTTK that is particularly important to the Dark Tower story, no great insight into the ending of the grand tale or really into the characters - it is what it is, an exciting and imaginative tale told using characters (well really only Roland as the rest of his ka-tet feature only very briefly) that we know very well and want to see in action.<br /><br />For me the pacing, atmosphere, and balance of mystery vs menace in this tale just hit perfectly and I got exactly what I wanted - hence the 5 stars up top.<br /><br />Will everyone love this book? No - but I don't think many will hate it.<br />Can you read it cold, without having read the other 7. Yes, but you'd be missing out on a lot. If you read it before book 5 and after book 4 (as the #4.5 indicates) then that would be fine too. But certainly it's a must for all Dark Tower fans, and if you've not read King's masterwork ... then get to it!<br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br /><br />......</span>
  <a data-text-id="12719161554679474433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_322084015" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322084015" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322084015?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=craptacular">craptacular</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=dark-tower">dark-tower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=uncle-stevie">uncle-stevie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=western">western</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322084015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10917116078535179900">Shenanigans! I cry shenanigans on Stephen King!<br/><br/>King put me through years of mental torture with <i>The Dark Tower</i> series, but I was able to forgive once he finally delivered a fitting ending to that saga. So I had a lot of concerns about him returning to the story of Roland. I worried that King had come down with a vicious case of Lucasitis that was going to have him tinkering with this story repeatedly. <br/><br/>However, King’s public statements indicated that it would not change the core <i>Dark Tower</i> story </span>
  <span id="freeText10917116078535179900" style="display:none">Shenanigans! I cry shenanigans on Stephen King!<br /><br />King put me through years of mental torture with <i>The Dark Tower</i> series, but I was able to forgive once he finally delivered a fitting ending to that saga. So I had a lot of concerns about him returning to the story of Roland. I worried that King had come down with a vicious case of Lucasitis that was going to have him tinkering with this story repeatedly. <br /><br />However, King’s public statements indicated that it would not change the core <i>Dark Tower</i> story and that it would just explore the long interlude between the fourth and fifth books. I’ve always had a big question regarding that since the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6595551" rel="nofollow noopener">Wizard &amp; Glass</a> had young Jake still being a new arrival to Mid-World and completely untrained as a gunslinger while Eddie and Susannah still had a lot to learn about carrying the heavy iron. When <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6595558" rel="nofollow noopener">Wolves of the Calla</a> picked up, all of them were stone cold bad asses after being on the path of the Beam for a good long while. It seemed like King was going to fill in that gap, and that was a story that I would have been interested in reading.<br /><br />I have to note here that <i>Wizard &amp; Glass</i> is my least favorite of the <i>Dark Tower</i> books. This was mainly for three reasons:<br /><br />1) After years of waiting, it didn’t advance the core story at all and instead focused on a flashback to young Roland.<br /><br />2) It involved a long tale with a character who really didn’t have anything to do with <i>DT</i> after that book.<br /><br />3) It was filled with fucking Wizard of Oz references.<br /><br />So what do we get in <i>The Wind Through the Keyhole</i>?<br /><br />1) A flashback story to young Roland.<br /><br />2) A flashback inside another flashback that tells a long tale about a character that has nothing to do with the rest of the <i>DT</i> story.<br /><br />3) A couple of <i>Wizard of Oz</i> references.<br /><br />Adding insult to injury, the main reason I read this wasn't addressed. Even though it’s supposed to be shortly after the ending of the fourth book, Jake is suddenly carrying a gun and going off ahead of the others and no one is worried because “He can take care of himself.” WHEN?? WHEN THE FUCK DID THAT HAPPEN? BECAUSE AS FAR AS I KNOW HE’S STILL THE KID WHO GOT KIDNAPPED AND NEARLY KILLED IN LUD, YET A WEEK OR TWO LATER HE’S JUST A GODDAMN GUNSLINGER WITH ABSOLUTELY NO TRAINING!! <br /><br />*ahem*<br /><br />So instead of getting the one damn question I wanted answered in this, the gunslingers are used as a framing device for Roland to tell them a story about his past that turns into him telling some little bastard a tale about another little bastard wandering off into the woods. <br /><br />Seriously, this could have been a fun offshoot short story or stories in larger collections someday, but putting them in a hardback and calling them <i>Dark Tower</i> just seems like the worst kind of bait and switch.<br /><br />I’m going to sell this one to a used book store and pretend it doesn’t exist.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10917116078535179900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2810064102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2810064102" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2810064102?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2810064102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15462558785896601983">The first fantasy series that I ever read was Stephen King's epic The Dark Tower. Looking back, it is by no means my favourite fantasy series however it opened the door for me to this wonderful genre that I've loved for 7-years. In similar fashion to the Russian doll-esque tale featured in The Wind Through the Keyhole, there is a story within a story with reference to my experiences too.<br/><br/>This review features one major spoiler for the series yet is referenced in the novel's forward by King himself</span>
  <span id="freeText15462558785896601983" style="display:none">The first fantasy series that I ever read was Stephen King's epic The Dark Tower. Looking back, it is by no means my favourite fantasy series however it opened the door for me to this wonderful genre that I've loved for 7-years. In similar fashion to the Russian doll-esque tale featured in The Wind Through the Keyhole, there is a story within a story with reference to my experiences too.<br /><br />This review features one major spoiler for the series yet is referenced in the novel's forward by King himself and a few minor spoilers. <br /><br />When I was a wide-eyed 9-year-old, my grandfather read Stephen King's Wizard and Glass to me, the book that chronologically precedes this entry. I remember adoring those times and they remain one of my most beloved memories. A train that challenged it's passengers to riddles? It was amazing. Instead of that book, I decided to re-experience this narrative as an older, wiser and uglier person. <br /><br />Here, the Gunslinger Roland presents a tale to his ka-tet (mid-world terminology for his crew) about a younger Roland who had just received his guns and the esteemed title of Gunslinger. <br /><br />"None of us can sleep," Jake said. "So tell us a story."<br /><br />Many years prior he meets a young lad called Bill who is about the age I was when my grandfather would read to me. Things are not looking great for Bill at present. His father has just been brutally murdered by a skin-man. This being is similar to what we are aware of through the myths and stories of werewolves but this version can change into many different animals as and when it deems necessary, such as a bear or a crocodile. This nightmare of a being has savagely attacked and mutilated far too many people in this quaint little town. From the minors to the working folk. Nobody is excluded from this creature's wrath. <br /><br />The skin-changer is the reason that 16-year-old Roland and his gunslinger companion Jamie DeCurry are here. They have been assigned a task to find and eliminate this threat. Bill escaped the massacre and witnessed the beast in it's changed, grotesque form. Roland wishes to question the young gentleman but if things couldn't get any worse a Starkblast is on the horizon. This is a behemothic tempest and storm concoction that can obliterate all and rip entire settlements to shreds. To keep Bill calm during the event after they are safely secure Roland promises to present one of his favourite tales that his mother used to tell him when he was a little lad called The Wind Through the Keyhole. <br /><br />"The stories we hear in our childhood are the ones we remember all our lives." - That's why I picked up this book again in memory of my grandfather as I felt it was fitting.<br /><br />It's not the finest The Dark Tower outing. I would say however though that it is definitely in the top-4. After the events of Wizard and Glass when the ka-tet leaves the land that was not Oz and before they arrive at Thunderclap and End-world, this story takes place. About 80-pages, comprising of the beginning and the end of the narrative is dedicated to the 'current day' Roland. These set the scene and then wrap up the happenings nicely before the gang is seen next in The Wolves of the Calla. To me, this was simply 'bubble-gum' reading and easy going rather than the sort of depth that comes later. It's great to be back with Eddie, Oy, Susannah, Roland, and Jake again. The banter between the ka-tet is as fluent, tight, humorous and natural as ever. It brought me many smiles after a long time away. Oy was always one of my favourite animal companions in fantasy books up there with Ghost (ASOI&amp;F) and Storm (F&amp;TF). It's a nice touch that Bully Bumblers are important throughout with the many upcoming storms.<br /><br />About a 100-pages are regarding younger Roland who has wisdom beyond his years. The rest of this metaphorical story cake is the portion about the magically haunting fairy tale that features Tim Stoutheart. <br /><br />The first story within a story is when Roland is sent on a mission with Jamie by his father, the legendary Gunslinger Stephen Deschain. A descendant of the line of Arthur Eld. There are a couple of neat sections here that enhance Roland's fathers already exceptional reputation. His body is a map of scars. This is the segment that grimdark fans will enjoy the most. It features a few heads being ripped off and devoured, also absolute catastrophic bloody murderous destruction, and a sometimes confused young Gunslinger. Naturally gifted, of course, but in these early escapades lacks the finesse during certain choices yet at the same time blows the metaphorical doors off with other intense analysis that then leads to very fine decisions. He's still a flawed work in progress and is living with the demon on his shoulder regarding the fact that he murdered his mother. <br /><br />The main meat on the narrative is the story within the story within the story. This section is a hauntingly beautiful dark fairy tale, yet even though terrible events happen throughout there is always an underlining degree of hope. This segment reminded me of the writing King did in one of his other fantasy endevours The Eyes of the Dragon and the Yarnsworld series by self-published author Benedict Patrick. I'll try not to say too much in detail about this part other than it features true love between family, betrayal, alcoholism, murder, a dragon, a forbidden forest, a mischevious fairy, and a couple of magicians. Readers of the main series will know one of these very well. It also features a Starkblast as do the other two storylines and to conclude, this section is enlightening, fulfilling and magical.<br /><br />I truly enjoyed reading this book again and devoured it within a handful of days. King states that this entry should be placed between book #4 and #5. I agree chronologically, yes, but to be read in that order, no. The reason being is that the majority of Wizard and Glass is a Roland flashback tale from his younger days, as it The Wind Through the Keyhole. As a first time reader, I would not wish to spend approximately 900 pages away from the main narrative. I read it originally after I had completed the main series and it sat well there. I'd either read it first or last in the series if I knew what I know now. A fine entry point but also a good final goodbye to the world to those who found the finale of The Dark Tower unfulfilling, leaving a bad taste in their mouth. In the latter order, it might make things seem a bit better. <br /><br />Thankee Sai for reading.<br /><br />Final note:- The few pages of artwork by Jae Lee, as it is with the graphic novels is absolutely spectacular!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15462558785896601983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=off-your-horse-and-drink-your-milk">off-your-horse-and-drink-your-milk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=group-or-buddy-read">group-or-buddy-read</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6168268-delee?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1420236136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15578888346272719772">Prologue: <br/><br/>No one said that the path to the beam, on the way to the Dark Tower was going to be this hard... Getting everyone on board for this on</span>
  <span id="freeText15578888346272719772" style="display:none">Prologue: <br><br>No one said that the path to the beam, on the way to the Dark Tower was going to be this hard... She CAN be kind of a liaaaaaaaaaar- and she is sort of insaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaane- so I should have known this wasn't going to be easy.<br><br>...but sweet 8 pound 6 ounce baby Jesus- I had nooooooo forewarning that one of my beloved Ka-tet was going to fight tooth and nail..not to read 4.5. Kemper you are a worthy opponent- We won the battle...this time- I have yet to see who will win the waaaaaaaaaaaaaaaar. Let me just say- I am glad you liked the rest of the series, because I don't think I would be strong enough to take you on- for books 5, 6, and 7....<br><br>On with the review:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445982926i/16728667.jpg" alt=" photo 974b46a1-28b7-45a8-8092-ad4692a3cb22_zpsysgdlav6.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Roland and his Ka-tet arrive at a river- and an elderly man- Bix- that operates the ferry assists them across the river.<br><br>A starkblast is coming and they will need to find shelter to wait out the storm. Roland tells them of an adventure in his youth to keep them occupied: The story of The Skin Man...and a story within the story- a tale that was told to Roland by his mother long ago.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445982926i/16728668.jpg" alt=" photo cdf744a2-9996-4517-bbf4-9a1e0c8d431f_zpshoabmtuz.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>First story:<br><br>Following the death of his mother- his father sends Roland and his friend Jamie De Curry to the town of Debaria on a mission to capture the Skin-Man.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445982926i/16728669.jpg" alt=" photo 9c1549db-3fec-4397-964e-1b6f8a461939_zps1gl4hp1p.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Second story:<br><br>Tim Ross lives with his mother Nell in a village who's property taxes are collected by a mysterious man called- The Covenant Man. Tim recently lost his father- who supposedly was killed by a dragon....but dragons may have been given a bad rap....read the book and you can decide for yourself.... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445982926i/16728670.png" alt=" photo e3d73804-9b80-4e2a-9b69-cb20dfaebdc5_zps6brpog9x.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I looooved THE WIND THROUGH THE KEYHOLE!!!! Sorry Kemper...I really did. For those of you that didn't like book 4....you may not like this one- but for those of you that did...this will be a pleasant journey.<br><br>The rest of the not so resistant buddies/Ka-tet- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/5879517-beverly" rel="nofollow noopener">Bev</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12618229-jeff" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeff</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6505947.Jason_Parent" rel="nofollow noopener">Jason</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420947607?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a>- Onward and upward....let the buddy-read continue.</span>

<div id="review_153651822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153651822" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153651822?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781451658903" href="/book/show/12106746-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153651822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5331065472060011303">While taking shelter from a storm along the Path of the Beam, Roland tells his ka-tet a story from his youth, about going up against a skin-man with Jamie DeCurry, in which he tells a frightened youth yet another story to bolster his courage...<br/><br/>First off, it pains me to give a Dark Tower book less than four stars but I thought this one was on par with Wizard and Glass.<br/><br/>The Wind Through the Keyhole is really three tales nested within one another. One features our beloved ka-tet, somewhere between t</span>
  <span id="freeText5331065472060011303" style="display:none">While taking shelter from a storm along the Path of the Beam, Roland tells his ka-tet a story from his youth, about going up against a skin-man with Jamie DeCurry, in which he tells a frightened youth yet another story to bolster his courage...<br /><br />First off, it pains me to give a Dark Tower book less than four stars but I thought this one was on par with Wizard and Glass.<br /><br />The Wind Through the Keyhole is really three tales nested within one another. One features our beloved ka-tet, somewhere between the green city from the end of Wizard and Glass and Wolves of the Calla, the second a tale from Roland's youth, and a third a fable from Roland's world. Since The Dark Tower is one of my all time favorite works, my expectations were extremely high and this book didn't live up to them.<br /><br />It isn't a bad book, though. Roland and the ka-tet are true to form. It didn't feel forced or tacked on. Rather, the stories felt natural and fleshed out both Roland's background and the mythology of Mid-World. I liked the Covenant Man quite a bit and the tale of the skin-man held my interest. If they weren't part of The Dark Tower, I probably would have rated them higher. Tim's tale reminded me of Eyes of the Dragon, one of Stephen King's more underrated works.<br /><br />I guess my main gripe was that there wasn't much in the way of gunslinging action. Sure, Roland got to strut his stuff a bit but I was hoping for something to explain the ka-tet's transformation between books four and five.<br /><br />Despite my gripes, I did enjoy The Wind Through the Keyhole and I was quite pleased that King left the ending open enough that he could stick another book or two in before the gang gets to the Calla. That'll have to satisfy my Dark Tower jones for now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5331065472060011303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1420947607" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420947607" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1420947607?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1420947607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer106225338828559371">Roland<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445883303i/16713710.png' width='340' height='290' alt='Man with No Name' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>and his sidekicks (called ka-tet) were minding their own business and kept going towards the Dark Tower when suddenly they had to interrupt their journey in a hurry, find some shelter and stay put for several days. Roland tells a story from his younger days to kill time (Skin Man). In that story he in turn had to kill some time and recounted another - this time fictional - story named The Wind Through the Keyhole. Confused yet? I hope the following picture helps.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445883139i/16713697._SX540_.jpg' width='340' height='260' alt='Russian nesting doll' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So there is a story inside </span>
  <span id="freeText106225338828559371" style="display:none">Roland<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445883303i/16713710.png" width="340" height="290" alt="Man with No Name" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>and his sidekicks (called ka-tet) were minding their own business and kept going towards the Dark Tower when suddenly they had to interrupt their journey in a hurry, find some shelter and stay put for several days. Roland tells a story from his younger days to kill time (Skin Man). In that story he in turn had to kill some time and recounted another - this time fictional - story named The Wind Through the Keyhole. Confused yet? I hope the following picture helps.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445883139i/16713697._SX540_.jpg" width="340" height="260" alt="Russian nesting doll" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So there is a story inside of a story inside of a story. The outer story takes place shortly after the events of Wizard and Glass. Despite King's reassurance in the Foreword it does contain some spoilers, albeit minor ones. It does not move the overall plot even by an inch. To cut to the chase, this part closely resembles the predecessor book I mentioned so if you like it you will like this story as well. As a corollary it follows that you can read this book at any time <b>after book 4</b>. <br><br>The middle story called Skin Man was the most interesting one. I was excited about it when I learned it was about Roland's days in Gilead shortly after the events of his flashback in Wizard and Glass. I hoped to see more Alain and Cuthbert, but got Jamie instead - and let us face it: Jamie is a pale shadow of these two. Other than this the tale was exciting and quite gruesome. <br><br>The inner story which gave the title to the whole book began slow and was quite boring and predictable for approximately one third of it. I can even give the exact place where it began to become interesting: with the appearance of the Tax Collector. <br><br>At this point I have to confess I hate the end of the whole series with a passion. I will not discuss it here, but I actually like this book. Yes, it does feel like King has some unused scenes from both last Roland's ka-tet travel (outer story), his flashback of book 4 (middle story), and an unrelated story loosely connected to mid-world (inner story), but it kinda sorta works - in a good way.<br><br>My final rating is <b>3.5 stars</b> rounded up. Why up? Because with the exception I mentioned above I was never bored with the read. I might feel 4 stars is a little bit high rating, but 3 stars are most definitely low. <br><br>P.S. Clint Eastwood in his prime would be THE actor to play Roland; nobody comes anywhere close - see the first picture as a proof. </span>
  <a data-text-id="106225338828559371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_260826257" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260826257" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/260826257?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781451658903" href="/book/show/12106746-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Dark Tower lovers and lovers of a well-written tale.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer260826257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12863935333062503900">Welcome to flashback town, population - <b>Wizard and Glass</b> and <b>The Wind Through the Keyhole</b>. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380367170i/719611._SX540_.jpg' width='375' height='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>(It's a terrible ride btw, unless you enjoy your head getting bashed over and over again.)<br/><br/>Wizard and Glass may have the record for length of flashback, but Wind Through the Keyhole goes Inception* on that flashback with a flashback** within a flashback. <br/><br/>*It's still accepted to reference Inception right?<br/><br/>**Okay, really it's a story within a flashback, but the story is a flashback to an even younger Roland te</span>
  <span id="freeText12863935333062503900" style="display:none">Welcome to flashback town, population - <b>Wizard and Glass</b> and <b>The Wind Through the Keyhole</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380367170i/719611._SX540_.jpg" width="375" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(It's a terrible ride btw, unless you enjoy your head getting bashed over and over again.)<br><br>Wizard and Glass may have the record for length of flashback, but Wind Through the Keyhole goes Inception* on that flashback with a flashback** within a flashback. <br><br>*It's still accepted to reference Inception right?<br><br>**Okay, really it's a story within a flashback, but the story is a flashback to an even younger Roland technically so...I'm going with it anyway.<br><br>As someone who has been reading this series chronologically (i.e., I've read the first four in the Dark Tower series, but have yet to read the last three), I'm having a really hard time picturing what it's like for a Dark Tower book to have plot progression with the main Ka-tet.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380367170i/719612.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book's been quite the divisive one and to be honest, I can't really disagree with what a lot of people have said who didn't like it nearly as much as I did. <br><br>So, having only read the first four books, reading The Wind Through the Keyhole was just a continuation of the last book, Wizard and Glass. I'm sure there are some things in Wind that I missed having not read the last three, and knowing this, of course we know our friends are going to be okay...right? Or are they? (yeah, they're fine)<br><br>And yet, that doesn't mean there's no dramatic tension. If you've read any of my reviews, you probably already know that <b>I really don't know what I'm talking about</b>. I didn't major in English and I've easily forgotten anything I've ever learned in high school or undergrad. <br><br>Given that, I want to talk about literary devices for a sec. Just because we know the ending already (well, not me), doesn't mean a story lacks tension. While we know they'll be "all right," one, we don't know how other characters will fair, and two, we're still looking for how they get back to "all right" because they're not at this point. So, it's really just a focus shift.<br><br>Okay, I'll quit talking about things I know nothing about...well, probably not.<br><br>We pick up just after the events from W&amp;G as our fearless Ka-tet is on their way from the glass tower in the first section titled "Starkblast." This doesn't last long, as you can imagine, and we're back into a flashback story from Roland's youth, which actually takes place just after the flashback from Wizard and Glass. This flashback is called "The Skin-Man."<br><br>Roland is sent on anther mission to another remote area of the world where a gunslinger is needed. Sadly, he takes another young gunslinger with him, not Alain and Cuthbert. I was SOOOO disappointed, I thought for sure we'd get those guys back.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380367170i/719613._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(Not sure if those are even Alain and Cuthbert, but the picture's pretty cool anyway.)<br><br>But wait, there's more...flashbacks that is. During the flashback in "The Skin-Man," Roland tells the titular tale, "The Wind Through the Keyhole." This tale actually makes up the bulk of the book and was easily my favorite part.<br><br>In "The Wind Through the Keyhole," King is in top form writing-wise. The story is independent and only mildly relates to either of the two other stories, but it's still a great one and I loved every minute of it.<br><br>It's a great old-timey adventure story about a kid who braves impossible odds to help his family. I have to say this again, the writing is top-notch (or tip top as the Swiss would say). He fits it to the story perfectly and puts me in awe at the talent this man possesses. He is the King in name and writing.<br><br>And just like a Matryoshka (or Russian nesting) doll, we head back to the first flashback in "The Skin-Man Part 2" and then back to our Ka-tet.<br><br>In summary, the story goes like this (not necessarily using the given titles): Ka-tet &gt; Flashback to Young Roland &gt; The Wind Through the Keyhole (main story) &gt; Flashback to Young Roland &gt; Ka-tet.<br><br>As much as I loved the main story, I didn't love the ending to the Young Roland flashback and the ka-tet portion was just a reference point if anything.<br><br>As someone who considers Wizard and Glass one of his all-time favorite books, I love me a good flashback. Not everyone does and I'll even admit that I thought this book would be a tale of the Ka-tet, not another flashback within a flashback. I'd still recommend this to readers of the Dark Tower and even non-readers may not be too confused. <br><br>4 out of 5 Stars (Highly Recommended)<br><br>Worth checking out: <a href="http://www.vulture.com/2012/04/ranking-all-62-stephen-king-books.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Here's a detailed list</a> of all of King's books from worst to best with semi-detailed descriptions of why the article's author thinks so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12863935333062503900" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1632170841" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1632170841" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1632170841?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781451658903" href="/book/show/12106746-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632170841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11582141012281780943">“The stories we hear in our childhood are the ones we remember all our lives.”<br/><br/>The story within a story within a story format is something that would put me off a book, yet it works so perfectly in The Wind Through the Keyhole. In what is effectively an additional backstory book within The Dark Tower series, we learn of another story from Roland’s younger years, of when Jamie De Curry and himself are sent to a town called Debaria to look into what has become known as The Skin-Man.<br/><br/>The Skin-Man is </span>
  <span id="freeText11582141012281780943" style="display:none">“The stories we hear in our childhood are the ones we remember all our lives.”<br /><br />The story within a story within a story format is something that would put me off a book, yet it works so perfectly in The Wind Through the Keyhole. In what is effectively an additional backstory book within The Dark Tower series, we learn of another story from Roland’s younger years, of when Jamie De Curry and himself are sent to a town called Debaria to look into what has become known as The Skin-Man.<br /><br />The Skin-Man is absolutely terrifying, a shapeshifter who takes on the form of numerous animals and goes on murderous rampages, easily wiping out entire families without breaking a sweat. I love these parts of the story, as Roland and Jamie try to narrow down who the culprit could be.<br /><br />Within this back story, Roland then tells a different story to a young kid as they are waiting in a jail cell - and this is the story given the name of The Wind Through the Keyhole. And it’s yet ANOTHER fascinating story that is essentially a dark fairy tale, full of magic and adventure. It actually reminds me a lot of The Eyes of the Dragon by King, although I would enjoy this one more!<br /><br />The format of this book works surprisingly well, and it helped that I was fully invested in all the different tales that were being told. Although this novel is not necessarily crucial to the main storyline of the series, it does of course teach us more about Roland, and I love the poignancy of the story with regards to Roland’s relationship with his mother. It always brings a tear to my eye.<br /><br />I also loved revisiting this at the end of the series. It was such a joy to be reacquainted with the ka-tet, even if only for a short spell, and it has really beautifully rounded off my reread of the series this year. 4.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11582141012281780943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570512052" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5792874057670514883">Re-Read 1/28/20:<br/><br/>Reading this in the official order of the Dark Tower series is a smart move. While little in Wizard and Glass or Wind Through the Keyhole can be appropriately called Plot Forward, the tales and tales and tales within tales across campfires are freaking appropriate. Murder and evil dudes are not all that a western is. :) <br/><br/>It helps that the tales in-between are pretty awesome, and these in Wind fit the bill perfectly. I think I liked Tim's tale more than the Skinwalker tale that fra</span>
  <span id="freeText5792874057670514883" style="display:none">Re-Read 1/28/20:<br /><br />Reading this in the official order of the Dark Tower series is a smart move. While little in Wizard and Glass or Wind Through the Keyhole can be appropriately called Plot Forward, the tales and tales and tales within tales across campfires are freaking appropriate. Murder and evil dudes are not all that a western is. :) <br /><br />It helps that the tales in-between are pretty awesome, and these in Wind fit the bill perfectly. I think I liked Tim's tale more than the Skinwalker tale that framed it, and Roland's Ka-Tet was just another frame, but a pleasant one. :)<br /><br /><br />Original Review:<br /><br />I've been a long-time fan of the Dark Tower series and I admit I was hugely curious to see a "middle" story pop out, long after the last book had been written. I was pleasantly surprised to find fully fleshed and embedded stories, three deep. It could have turned very complicated and burdensome, but it just worked. I really wanted to see a novel, even a 4.5 novelette, deepen and expound upon Roland's strange "more real than real" land, but while I was disappointed in that regards, what I did find were characters I really enjoyed and a "soft" exploration of the world and its honor, (or lack of). <br /><br />It was a fairy tale (for a kid who's Pa had been gored by a shapeshifter) within a fairy tale (to pass the time while weathering a hellish storm) within a fairy tale (for us). It was by no means a series of epic tales, although it was still couched within the longer progression of the Dark Tower, so you could make the argument.<br />Could someone enjoy this book without reading the rest of the series? I think they can do so, very much. There was little enough spoilers for the rest of the tale, nor elements that needed to be built up and explored very thoroughly indeed or it loses the climatic flavor.<br />The novel was simply fun and enjoyable. :)</span>

Jim Beam.”<br><br>“Oh, this surprise’ll <i>captivate</i> ya, ya brawlin’, boozin’ sidewinder.” She laughed maniacally to herself and turned away from the man.<br><br>After feeding branches into the fire, the tall blonde strode around the adobe for a few minutes and then announced that it was time for a story.<br><br>The strapping man groaned.<br><br>“What was that, my cully? Didn’t quite catch that”<br><br>The man’s face fell. “Another story? I’m tar’d! The last damn story ya done told, lasted fer days and we had ta beg ya fer bathroom breaks. No, I ain’t listenin’ to no stories. No sai, I ain’t.”<br><br>The sound of a pair of pistols cocking at the back of head, almost made the man soil himself.<br><br>“Is there a problem here, Quick Draw?” The second smaller woman’s voice cut through the chill and flickering shadows like an ice pick.<br><br>“There ain’t no problem, Rootin’ Tootin’.” She turned to the man. “Is there?”<br><br>Rootin’ Tootin’ eyed the man. “Cause if there’s a problem, I can get the ball gag and hand cuffs outta my saddle bag.”<br><br>“There ain’t no problem,” muttered the man.<br><br>“Good, cause yer gonna like this story, cuz it’s two stories in one, it’s clever like one of them there Russian Matryoshka dolls.”<br><br>The tall woman sighed and started her tale, “Picture a peach. Down on the farm. Times are tough…”<br><br>The man put his head down, hat over his eyes and started to weep softly and then drifted off into sleep, until he was awakened by a hard kick to the ribs…<br><br>Both women cackled.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451919300i/17621558._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736744303" />
    <a title="Andre Gonzalez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53583787-andre-gonzalez"><img alt="Andre Gonzalez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546573233p2/53583787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1736744303?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andre Gonzalez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andre Gonzalez" href="/user/show/53583787-andre-gonzalez">Andre Gonzalez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736744303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11770809531570416359">The writing was stellar in this book, telling a story within a story has to be pretty difficult. While the story was entertaining, I'm having trouble seeing why it was necessary. I'm reading the DT series through for the first time and thought I would respect the order where this book fell, and feel like I could have done without this pitstop that takes away from the main journey. That being said, I look forward to starting Wolves of the Calla to get back on track!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1423462585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423462585" />
    <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12058788-2"><img alt="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589380555p2/12058788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1423462585?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ɗẳɳ  2.☊" href="/user/show/12058788-2">Ɗẳɳ  2.☊</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781444731705" href="/book/show/12203201-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=western">western</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12058788-2?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1423462585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4484943084205755723"><b>★★★★☆½</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“It was the best of times, it was the worst of times…it was the spring of hope, it was the winter of despair.”</i>
</b> <br/><br/>Whoops! Wrong quote there, but it seems somewhat appropriate for such a polarizing little book. I’m truly shocked at how varied the ratings are on this one, even amongst friends whose opinions I trust. I typically avoid all the .5 stories, since they’re usually just pointless filler, and seeing some of those one star ratings out there was not especially encouraging. Our fearle</span>
  <span id="freeText4484943084205755723" style="display:none"><b>★★★★☆½</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“It was the best of times, it was the worst of times…it was the spring of hope, it was the winter of despair.”</i>
</b> <br /><br />Whoops! Wrong quote there, but it seems somewhat appropriate for such a polarizing little book. I’m truly shocked at how varied the ratings are on this one, even amongst friends whose opinions I trust. I typically avoid all the .5 stories, since they’re usually just pointless filler, and seeing some of those one star ratings out there was not especially encouraging. Our fearless leader; however, insisted I tag along, so I reluctantly caved to the peer pressure. Boy, am I ever glad that I did!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Time is a keyhole, he thought as he looked up at the stars. Yes, I think so. We sometimes bend and peer through it. And the wind we feel on our cheeks when we do—the wind that blows through the keyhole—is the breath of all the living universe.”</i>
</b><br /><br />As many have stated, this one is a story within a story within a story. Sounds confusing, but it's actually not. It all begins where book four left off. Our ka-tet is still on the path of the beam, but a powerful storm forces our group to seek shelter. While we wait out the storm, Roland tells of an adventure from his youth. Properly told, I might add, in the first person this time around.<br /><br />The story he tells, occurs fairly soon after the Susan Delgado flashback from book four. There’s talk of a <i>“skin-man”</i> or shape-shifter plaguing the small town of Debaria, not far from Gilead. Roland’s father doubts the rumors are true, he believes it’s probably just some lunatic wearing animal skins, but sends Roland and his friend Jamie, another young gunslinger with a bit of dead fish personality, to investigate nonetheless.<br /><br />The day after they arrive in Debaria the gunslingers are taken to the scene of a <i>grizzly</i> mass murder. Roland devises a plan to flesh out the perpetrator, and sets Jamie and the local Sheriff to the task. He returns to town with the lone survivor, a young boy, and waits for the others. To pass the time, and keep the boy’s mind off the horrific events he’s witnessed, Roland tells of another tale.<br /><br /><i>The Wind Through the Keyhole</i> is a very old story told to Roland by his mother. It occurred once upon a bye, back in the days of dragons, and endless forest, a time when Maerlyn himself walked the earth. It essentially revolves around a brave young boy named Tim, the lengths to which he would go to save his mother, and a mysterious Covenant Man scheming in the background.<br /><br />Wind is the central theme that links all the tales; from the starkblast, to the simoom, to the wind through the keyhole. As someone who's yet to read the entire series I thought this book held some nice intrigue, and provided a few juicy tidbits that added to the Dark Tower lore. As feared, it doesn’t really advance our long journey; however, that's not to say that there weren't some interesting developments. We actually get to meet Maerlyn, and learn a little more of the Red King, and the world building and folklore are superb throughout. Most importantly though, the story itself was engaging, start to finish.<br /><br />I've read a lot of those negative reviews, and the complaints seem to revolve around a few key issues. One, this story didn't address the long gap between books four and five. Two, our current ka-tet was almost entirely absent from the tale. Three, Jamie is a poor substitute for Roland’s original ka-tet in the Skin-Man story. Four, the Wind through the Keyhole is an old story with many unknown characters that are unimportant to the Dark Tower. <br /><br />Essentially it all felt like a case of bait-and-switch, where fans were promised one thing, but King delivers something entirely different. I get that, I understand those frustrations, I really do, but setting aside all those feelings and judging the story strictly on its merits I couldn't truthfully call this anything other than a success. And frankly, I enjoyed the hell out of it. Maybe it was a case of the right place, right time; call it what you will, but this was some of the most fun I've had in Mid-World since book two! <br /><br />It just goes to show when he writes concisely, and cuts out all that needless filler, uncle Stevie can still spin one hell of a yarn. This has actually renewed my enthusiasm for the series. I hope things get back on track, and I can't wait to see where it all leads! I may even have to reverse my stance on .5 stories. I see how it can be fun to check back in on a familiar world even if it's not to advance the overall plot line.<br /><br />4.5 stars. Minus ½ a star for the fairly predictable early sections of the WTTK tale and rushed ending to the Skin-Man. Overall though, I loved it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Stories take a person away. If they’re good ones, that is. It is a good one?”<br />“Yes. I always thought so, anyway.”<br />“Then tell it.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The rest of our ka-tet, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322998390" rel="nofollow noopener">Stepheny</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/12618229-jeff" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeff</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420236136" rel="nofollow noopener">Delee</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1422231493" rel="nofollow noopener">Jason</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420947607" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a> jumped in for one book only. Karly sat this one out, and Kat &amp; Bev are still lost somewhere along the path of the beam.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4484943084205755723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2815196906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2815196906" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2815196906?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2815196906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6150800709998024152">Stephen King concluded his brilliant epic Dark Tower series in 2004. In 2012 he returned to this universe to add The Wind Through the Keyhole, set in the story between the events of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5096.Wizard_and_Glass__The_Dark_Tower___4_' title='Wizard and Glass (The Dark Tower, #4) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wizard and Glass</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4978.Wolves_of_the_Calla__The_Dark_Tower___5_' title='Wolves of the Calla (The Dark Tower, #5) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Wolves of the Calla</a>.<br/><br/>This is a story within a story being told as a recollection of Roland. While many fans of the series lamented and were even angered by King’s failing to add a substantive chapter to the series, this succeeds in adding colorful detail to Roland’s past – which truth be told is a</span>
  <span id="freeText6150800709998024152" style="display:none">Stephen King concluded his brilliant epic Dark Tower series in 2004. In 2012 he returned to this universe to add The Wind Through the Keyhole, set in the story between the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5096.Wizard_and_Glass__The_Dark_Tower___4_" title="Wizard and Glass (The Dark Tower, #4) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Wizard and Glass</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4978.Wolves_of_the_Calla__The_Dark_Tower___5_" title="Wolves of the Calla (The Dark Tower, #5) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Wolves of the Calla</a>.<br><br>This is a story within a story being told as a recollection of Roland. While many fans of the series lamented and were even angered by King’s failing to add a substantive chapter to the series, this succeeds in adding colorful detail to Roland’s past – which truth be told is a big part of my fascination with the series.<br><br>The first story has Roland recounting an adventure from his past, shortly after his mother was killed and where he and Jamie are on the trail of a murderous skin changer.<br><br>The second tale is of this earlier Roland telling a legend from their past to a young boy who is scared. This is about Tim, a semi-legendary figure and his adventures with a dragon, a tiger and of a mysterious magic user.<br><br>King’s depiction of a world that “has moved on” with golden references to pop culture and myth and legend and literature is, to me, the best part of his storytelling. I also love the way he uses recurring characters throughout his canon and fans will note some important connecting scenes in this one.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557678671i/27495443._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_3110999444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3110999444" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3110999444?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/28004160-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3110999444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6168118942053702258">This is one of the "short stories" that flesh out the world(s) and characters of the <i>Dark Tower</i> series by Stephen King. It was written much later, but I'm glad that my buddy-reader and I are reading it in chronological order nevertheless.<br/><br/>Just like in the 4th volume of the series, this is a story-within-the-story that features yet another story within that.<br/>Roland and his "new" Ka-tet are on their way to the Outer Baronies when they have to seek shelter from a storm after crossing a river. In orde</span>
  <span id="freeText6168118942053702258" style="display:none">This is one of the "short stories" that flesh out the world(s) and characters of the <i>Dark Tower</i> series by Stephen King. It was written much later, but I'm glad that my buddy-reader and I are reading it in chronological order nevertheless.<br><br>Just like in the 4th volume of the series, this is a story-within-the-story that features yet another story within that.<br>Roland and his "new" Ka-tet are on their way to the Outer Baronies when they have to seek shelter from a storm after crossing a river. In order to pass the time, Roland tells of another adventure he had as a young man. <br>Thus, the first story-within-the-story takes place shortly after Roland had been tricked into killing his mother. He and another member of his old Ka-tet, Jamie, are sent to Debaria where a shapeshifter keeps killing people - and in horrible ways. There is one survivor of the newest massacre, a little boy, and the night before he's supposed to identify the murderer, Roland calms the terrified child by telling him a story from <i>Magic Tales of the Eld</i>, bedtime stories Roland's mother used to tell him. <br>This way, the reader learns of Tim Ross/Stoutheart and his trials and tribulations after his father's death that include an abusive stepfather, a tax collector, fairies, dragons, wizards, white as well as black magic and a very special tiger.<br>Afterwards, we are briefly back to identify the killer and see Roland getting a very special message that he also discusses briefly with Susannah, Eddie and Jake before they continue on their way to the Dark Tower after the storm has finally passed.<br><br>This is the cover of another edition and I think it's the prettiest thing ever. REALLY love that tiger's look and details such as the pendant. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580234375i/28858674.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After having read the previous book, I must say that this clearly shows that King is able to get to the point much more quickly while still fleshing out a full world. Yes, there are once again three layers of stories told (the present with the new Ka-tet, the flashback to Roland's old Ka-tet and the bedtime story), but it works and engages the reader, the events didn't drag and I found myself puzzling over the shapeshifter as much as about what happened to Tim.<br><br>Very nice addition though it didn't add anything to the flow of events in the actual series. Sometimes it's nice to just stay in one place for a while and immerse yourself in some crime and/or mythology (and yes, there was yet another puzzle piece about Walter/Marten/...).</span>
  <a data-text-id="6168118942053702258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
