        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322998390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13175609564160373217">*My shiny new updated review for my re-read*<br/><br/>As I look back on our long and treacherous journey I am not shocked to see that there have been some casualties. I wish I could say I was, but the Quest for the Dark Tower has claimed many of lives. Aye, so it has. We lost one to demon sex, one to Japanese comics, one who ran so far ahead of us without looking back and one just kind of backed slowly away… ( I get that last one a lot…I can’t imagine why!) But as we have lost some, we have also gained so</span>
  <span id="freeText13175609564160373217" style="display:none">*My shiny new updated review for my re-read*<br /><br />As I look back on our long and treacherous journey I am not shocked to see that there have been some casualties. I wish I could say I was, but the Quest for the Dark Tower has claimed many of lives. Aye, so it has. We lost one to demon sex, one to Japanese comics, one who ran so far ahead of us without looking back and one just kind of backed slowly away… ( I get that last one a lot…I can’t imagine why!) But as we have lost some, we have also gained some. And we have one who has tried her best to keep up but is now playing catch up instead.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1423462585?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dastardly Dan</a> was <i>by far</i> my hardest battle. I think I would have had an easier time pulling the teeth of a toddler while stealing the poor thing’s candy too. I thought for a while he wasn't going to commit but in the end I managed to gently persuade him into it. Clearly, this is a victory. 4 stars from Dan is not an easy feat! <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420947607?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a> decided to join us for this adventure! There is also, of course, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420236136?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Rootin' Tootin' Pistol Packin' Ass Whuppin’ Virgin Blood Drinkin' Delee</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1421823557?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Jumpin’ Jeff</a> and our favorite newbie, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1422231493?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Black Jackin’ Jason</a>! <br /><br />This book is one of my all-time favorites. It is so beautifully written and so intricate. As it has been explained in 827320821 other reviews, this is a story within a story within a story. Roland and his Ka-Tet are waiting out a Starkblast and Jake wants to hear a story from Roland’s childhood. Roland obliges and explains what happened to him after leaving Mejis. His father sends him on a quest- a quest believed to be a bunch of smoke and mirrors; a skin-man is terrorizing a nearby town and he sends Roland and some friends to investigate to get them out of his hair.<br /><br />But when Roland gets there he meets Bill- a terrified child whose whole family was brutally murdered and eaten(for the most part) by the alleged skin-man. While Roland waits for suspects to be gathered he decides to tell Bill a story. This story was one that is older than time itself, according to Roland, a tale told to Roland by his own mother. The name of this tale you ask? Why, the Wind Through the Keyhole, of course!<br /><br /><b>“Once upon a bye, before your grandfather’s grandfather was born, on the edge of an unexplored wilderness called the Endless Forest, there lived a boy named Tim” </b><br /><br />And so begins my most treasured adventure. Wind tells us about Tim Stoutheart. Tim must go on a quest of his own into the deepest parts of the forest in hopes of finding some answers… Will he find what he’s looking for? Will he be able to get back to his poor mother in time? Is the magic real? Are the dragons really gone? And what truly happened to Maerlyn?<br /><br />But more importantly, will we find out what happened to Bill’s family? Is the skin-man truly able to change from one animal skin to another? Or is it just some sick twisted game for a bored mine-worker? Will the killer be brought to justice?<br /><br />And not to be forgotten- will our favorite Ka-Tet be able to withstand the wind of the Starkblast? <br /><br />I know that not all of my Tet was originally on board to read this book with me but I am glad that the ones who chose to did. Sharing a favorite book is by far one of the greatest feelings in the world. And the icing on top is when they love it…even if they don’t love it as much as I do! I do understand that my <s>love</s> obsession over certain books/series is a taaaad ridiculous sometimes. But there are times that books change who you are as a person. And this is one of those books.<br /><br />I’ll leave you with a few of my favorite quotes.<br /><br /><b>“In the end, the wind takes everything, doesn't it? And why not? Why other? If the sweetness of our lives did not depart, there would be no sweetness at all.”&gt;<br /><br /><b>“A person’s never too old for stories. Man and boy, girl and woman, we live for them.” </b><br /><br />And lastly,<br /><br /><b>“Time is a keyhole, he thought as he looked up at the stars. Yes, I think so. We sometimes bend and peer through it. And the wind we feel on our cheeks when we do - the wind that blows through the keyhole- is the breath of all the living universe.”</b><br /><br /><br /></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13175609564160373217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_163302962" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163302962" />
    <a title="Trudi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi"><img alt="Trudi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446613110p2/1416912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163302962?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trudi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trudi" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi">Trudi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781451658903" href="/book/show/12106746-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=the-big-letdown">the-big-letdown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=dark-tower">dark-tower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163302962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13186768256517750162"><br/>Sigh. Well, it's finished. I will now try and express some of my deep disappointments here even though it will hurt me to do so. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322084015' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kemper's review</a> captures much of what frustrated me and left me feeling cheated by the whole affair. To be promised another Dark Tower installment and offered this underwhelming book in its place, so loosely tethered to the source material as to feel as if someone else wrote it, a comical pastiche in parts that tries too hard to be Dark Tower worthy -- well, it just le</span>
  <span id="freeText13186768256517750162" style="display:none"><br />Sigh. Well, it's finished. I will now try and express some of my deep disappointments here even though it will hurt me to do so. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322084015" rel="nofollow noopener">Kemper's review</a> captures much of what frustrated me and left me feeling cheated by the whole affair. To be promised another Dark Tower installment and offered this underwhelming book in its place, so loosely tethered to the source material as to feel as if someone else wrote it, a comical pastiche in parts that tries too hard to be Dark Tower worthy -- well, it just leaves a girl wanting to cry. <br /><br />I guess I should have read the dust jacket more closely. Maybe if I had gone into this knowing full well that this <u>IS NOT</u> a Dark Tower story, but rather a bedtime story from Roland's youth (ripped from the pages of <i>Magic Tales of the Eld</i>) my disappointment could have been more tempered. <br /><br />As it stands, we get a paltry 35 pages of Roland, Jake, Susannah, Eddie and Oy (that's not even a story -- it's just used as a framing device for the rest of the book). We get about 100 pages of a Young Roland Adventure -- a monster of the week story that reminded me of Sam and Dean Winchester and an episode of <i>Supernatural</i> set in Mid-World (awesome idea and if Stephen King ever wants to write the Winchesters into the Dark Tower landscape I would probably die from fangirl shock syndrome). In this context however, it didn't work for me. I'm not the biggest fan of Young Roland anyway, and Young Roland in the first person is barely recognizable. It could have been anyone telling that story. <br /><br />The remaining 160 or so pages is a fairytale featuring a young boy on a quest to save his mother, that may be vaguely set in Mid-World, but has so very little to do with ANYTHING Dark Tower or ka-tet as to leave one itchy and sore. It's a pleasing enough story, but all while I was reading it, all I could think about was 'the gang' and wishing I were back with them, walking with them, adventuring with them. When Stephen King announced he had another Dark Tower story to tell, I believed him, why wouldn't I? It made sense to me that there would be LOADS of smaller stories of ka-tet adventures that did not make it into the 7 book magnum opus, but nevertheless deserve to be told anyway. I want those stories, dammit! <b>Pretty pleeeeeeease</b>, can't I have those stories? <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13186768256517750162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau"><img alt="Ashley Daviau" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599784716p2/35915119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1084118541?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Daviau" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Daviau" href="/user/show/35915119-ashley-daviau">Ashley Daviau</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781451658910" href="/book/show/15015023-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1084118541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5210527356673405178">I think this is honestly my least favourite book out of the Dark Tower series. Now that doesn't mean that I didn't love it, I just didn't love it quite as much as the rest of the series. <br/><br/>I find in some places that it gets a bit long and my mind constantly wandered and wondered what would happen in the next book rather than focusing on this book and what it had to offer. <br/><br/>I feel like I'm making it sound like a terrible book and that's definitely not the case, I mean I did give it five stars! I jus</span>
  <span id="freeText5210527356673405178" style="display:none">I think this is honestly my least favourite book out of the Dark Tower series. Now that doesn't mean that I didn't love it, I just didn't love it quite as much as the rest of the series. <br /><br />I find in some places that it gets a bit long and my mind constantly wandered and wondered what would happen in the next book rather than focusing on this book and what it had to offer. <br /><br />I feel like I'm making it sound like a terrible book and that's definitely not the case, I mean I did give it five stars! I just find it lacks a little bit of a punch, that's all. <br /><br />I can't say which way I prefer reading this one now that I've done it both ways. Reading it after reading the original 7 books has its merits but so does reading it between books 4 and 5! </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184310992" />
    <a title="Kevin Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405472-kevin-michael"><img alt="Kevin Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1192106739p2/405472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184310992?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevin Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevin Michael" href="/user/show/405472-kevin-michael">Kevin Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184310992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17738291553934004544">It was good to be back in Midworld, if only for a short visit. This book is three stories in one, and those looking for an expansion of the quest for the Tower will be disappointed. Only the frame story contains Roland and his ka-tet from our world. Roland tells Jake, Eddie, and Susannah a tale from his days as a young gunslinger, but even that story is just another frame for the true story: The Wind Through the Keyhole, a fairytale Roland's mother told him when he was a young boy. The fairytale</span>
  <span id="freeText17738291553934004544" style="display:none">It was good to be back in Midworld, if only for a short visit. This book is three stories in one, and those looking for an expansion of the quest for the Tower will be disappointed. Only the frame story contains Roland and his ka-tet from our world. Roland tells Jake, Eddie, and Susannah a tale from his days as a young gunslinger, but even that story is just another frame for the true story: The Wind Through the Keyhole, a fairytale Roland's mother told him when he was a young boy. The fairytale tells the story of young Tim Ross, who must brave a dark forest, a possible encounter with a dragon, magic, and worst of all, an abusive stepfather--all during a quest to save his mother. The story is beautiful, magical, and terrifying, and Constant Readers will quickly recognize The Covenant Man for who he really is.<br /><br />I am both happy and sad to say that this is far better than the last three "official" books in the Dark Tower series. It's a shame that King didn't wait for inspiration to strike before concluding Roland's quest. "The Wind Through the Keyhole" is proof that he still has plenty of brilliant stories to tell, and that he is at his best when he writes for himself, not out of obligation to his impatient fans. I would welcome a dozen more of these Midworld tales from one of the greatest storytellers of our time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17738291553934004544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_153813592" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153813592" />
    <a title="Chris " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1956959-chris"><img alt="Chris " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502408626p2/1956959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153813592?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781451658903" href="/book/show/12106746-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=2012-read-owned">2012-read-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=read-owned-hardcover">read-owned-hardcover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153813592" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15391353729772167237">....<br/><br/>Uummmmm. What do I say? For as long as I've been on GR, I've seen the debate on the Dark Tower. Which story era is more enjoyable? The "present day (sorta)" ka-tet of Roland, Susannah, Eddie, Jake, and Oy. Or the "Young Roland" era when he ran with Alain, Cuthbert, and Jamie?<br/><br/>So as I'm about to start this book, I find out that many of the "present day" crews are disappointed because we get a little time with the ka-tet, only to have the story shift back in time with Roland telling another sto</span>
  <span id="freeText15391353729772167237" style="display:none">....<br /><br />Uummmmm. What do I say? For as long as I've been on GR, I've seen the debate on the Dark Tower. Which story era is more enjoyable? The "present day (sorta)" ka-tet of Roland, Susannah, Eddie, Jake, and Oy. Or the "Young Roland" era when he ran with Alain, Cuthbert, and Jamie?<br /><br />So as I'm about to start this book, I find out that many of the "present day" crews are disappointed because we get a little time with the ka-tet, only to have the story shift back in time with Roland telling another story of his youth, much like Wizard &amp; Glass. That book seems to be either a least favorite or a most favorite with everyone. With me, it was a most favorite. So while they were lamenting the return to the early Roland days, I was excited.<br /><br />But in the end, Ka got me too. King pulled a double switch on us, giving us a little Roland story within the Ka-tet story, only to have THAT one shift to a storytelling situation about a kid we never heard of from even further back. And I'm like, wtf? It's ok for a little bit, but it takes up half the damn book.<br /><br />The actual story "The Wind Through the Keyhole" is this thing, a fable about a kid disguised and sold as a Dark Tower novel. Ok, so there are some Midworld references and sayings and society stuff built in, so I can see that. It was Midworldian. It was rather interesting to see some stuff in the long ago, before the world moved on. <br /><br />But if it's always like that, I can see why it moved on. It was boring. That story didn't even feel like a King story. It wasn't bad. It started out alright. By the end it was even engaging. But the middle slogged on quite a bit to the point that I found my mind drifting. <br /><br />Then we switch back to Young Roland and get a quick wrap up on that story, which was very intriguing and enjoyable. And finally, we switch back up to modern Roland and Ka-tet, getting a wrap up on it too. Which wasn't a wrap up as much as a "ok, we're done screwing around, let's get on with it" that leads into Book 5.<br /><br />Crap, it was like reading <i>Inception</i>. Only not as good.<br /><br />Half this book is 5-star material (Young Roland story, Modern Roland interlude). The other half of the book is 3-star (with some boring 2-star fairy chasing in the middle). We'll average it out and call it 4. I'm being generous, but it IS a Dark Tower related book. I won't call it part of the main series though. It's an extra, like <i>The Little Sisters of Eluria</i> or the graphic novel series.<br /><br />ETA (1/27/2013): The more this book has settled in, the more I am bothered by my overly generous 4-star review. It simply doesn't deserve it. A 4-star should not leave a bad taste in my mouth 8 months after I've finished it.<br /><br />It's worth reading, but simply does not measure up to the rest of the series, period. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15391353729772167237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14332778127963587095">As a bridge between <i>Wizard and Glass</i> & <i>Wolves of the Calla</i>, this book couldn't be more perfect. It draws on the dark, down-to-earth nostalgia of growing up in a harsh, mean world that <i>Wizard</i> did beautifully, but it also introduces the bat-shit crazy, heady material of alternate dimensions and dense mythos that <i>Wolves</i> began introducing in its later pages. So it may not move the overall plot forward, but it's not supposed to. That plot already ended eight years ago. This is a bridge book. A book m</span>
  <span id="freeText14332778127963587095" style="display:none">As a bridge between <i>Wizard and Glass</i> &amp; <i>Wolves of the Calla</i>, this book couldn't be more perfect. It draws on the dark, down-to-earth nostalgia of growing up in a harsh, mean world that <i>Wizard</i> did beautifully, but it also introduces the bat-shit crazy, heady material of alternate dimensions and dense mythos that <i>Wolves</i> began introducing in its later pages. So it may not move the overall plot forward, but it's not supposed to. That plot already ended eight years ago. This is a bridge book. A book meant for newcomers to the series to read as The Dark Tower 4.5, and in that head-space, it's up there with the best of King's work. </span>

<div id="review_163298817" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163298817" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163298817?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781451658903" href="/book/show/12106746-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_nook">ebook_nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=dark-tower">dark-tower</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163298817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6519696372867623335">3.5 Stars <br/>Believe it or not, there was a time when I hadn't read the Dark Tower series... but we don't talk about that. It's a painful time in my history, and polite company lets me keep my shame to myself. But I mention it because since stepping foot into the Tower multiverse, everything changed. I thought I was a Stephen King fan until I read the Dark Tower series, but I had no idea how much I could love King and his books. I <i>adore</i> this series. No other series or book can claim a higher spot i</span>
  <span id="freeText6519696372867623335" style="display:none">3.5 Stars <br />Believe it or not, there was a time when I hadn't read the Dark Tower series... but we don't talk about that. It's a painful time in my history, and polite company lets me keep my shame to myself. But I mention it because since stepping foot into the Tower multiverse, everything changed. I thought I was a Stephen King fan until I read the Dark Tower series, but I had no idea how much I could love King and his books. I <i>adore</i> this series. No other series or book can claim a higher spot in my heart (not even Harry Potter, though that's a very close second), so when I learned that there would be a new book in the series, I SQUEE'd all over the damn place. Messy clean-up, but so worth it. <br /><br />Dark Tower is bittersweet. It is. But that's one of my favorite things about King; he makes it real. So I couldn't wait, nay... COULD. NOT. WAIT. to read the shit out of this book and finally see the ka-tet again. To go on another adventure with them, to see what this new interlude holds... despite knowing ka-shume is coming down the path of the beam for them. But then... I admit to feeling a bit cheated after I started. Maybe that's not fair, probably not, because had I read the book description, I'd have known that likely wasn't going to be what I'd get... But those of you who know me well, those who share my khef, do it please ya, will know that I wouldn't want to know, that I'd want to just go where Ka's wind blows. And so I did... but I can't help wanting more of Roland, Eddie, Susannah, Jake, and Oy. <br /><br />As a ka-tet book, low marks for this one because there's just so little of them here... but as a Mid-World/multiverse book, high marks, because there's a lot here in that regard, and it's quite interesting to piece together. <br /><br />What we have here is a story within a story within a story. Not my favorite thing. I love Wizard and Glass, but the Mejis flashback storyline is long. W&amp;G is my least favorite of the series for this reason, and I always get to a point where I'm ready for the Young Roland story to be done so I can get back to Present Roland. But saying it's my least favorite is not saying much, because every book in the series is fantastic in its own way. <br /><br />So coming on the heels of Wizard and Glass, in internal story setting order, is The Wind Through the Keyhole, where our ka-tet takes shelter from a starkblast and has another episode from Roland's seemingly endless cache of Adventure Stories From My Youth and Other Relevant Tales from Before The World Moved On. <br /><br />The first story Roland tells is of being sent on another mission by his father to take care of what's rumored to be a Skin-Man (a shapeshifter) terrorizing one of the baronies. Within this story is the story from which this book takes its title, which is the story of Tim Ross and his encounter with the Covenant Man, whose horse is called Blackie. Just sayin'. This story ties into both the Young Roland story, and the Present Roland story... in different ways, which was interesting. <br /><br />These two stories make up the bulk of the book, which is short (for King) to begin with. But these are interesting, particularly Tim's The Wind Through The Keyhole, because of how other multiverse books might, and probably do, connect with it. I counted quite a few references to other books in the three stories, including Eyes of the Dragon, The Talisman, and Desperation, just to name a few. <br /><br />I won't go into much more detail, since everyone should read it for themselves. Overall for me, this was worth the read, although my heart still wanted more of Roland, Eddie, Susannah, Jake, and Oy. Maybe... Maybe Gan will bless King with another Dark Tower book? <br /><br />A girl can dream...</span>
  <a data-text-id="6519696372867623335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1305966070" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305966070" />
    <a title="Kyriakos Sorokkou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5927877-kyriakos-sorokkou"><img alt="Kyriakos Sorokkou" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585580294p2/5927877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1305966070?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kyriakos Sorokkou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kyriakos Sorokkou" href="/user/show/5927877-kyriakos-sorokkou">Kyriakos Sorokkou</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444731729" href="/book/show/17323860-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1305966070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2306172325921456392"><u>
  <b>DTProject2017 | Book 4.5</b>
</u><br/><br/>Many people didn't like this book mainly for two reasons:<br/><br/>1] It resembles the previous book (4) which is mainly a flashback in Roland's youth and many people hated that book because it was mainly a flashback, so they hated this book as well.<br/>2] The main story of the book is actually a fairy tale and doesn't add any progress to the core narrative, which is something I don't mind since I'm more interested in Roland's past than his quest to the Dark Tower.<br/><br/>This book reminds</span>
  <span id="freeText2306172325921456392" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>DTProject2017 | Book 4.5</b>
</u><br /><br />Many people didn't like this book mainly for two reasons:<br /><br />1] It resembles the previous book (4) which is mainly a flashback in Roland's youth and many people hated that book because it was mainly a flashback, so they hated this book as well.<br />2] The main story of the book is actually a fairy tale and doesn't add any progress to the core narrative, which is something I don't mind since I'm more interested in Roland's past than his quest to the Dark Tower.<br /><br />This book reminds me a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6794.Cloud_Atlas" title="Cloud Atlas by David Mitchell" rel="nofollow noopener">Cloud Atlas</a> which was a babushka book. <br />Here we have 3 instead of 6 stories. The first time I read it (2013) I haven't read or heard of the Cloud Atlas so I didn't see any resemblance. <br /><br />It is a story, within a story, within a story, or to make it clearer,<br />It is a fairy tale, within a flashback, within a main story, or to make it even clearer :)<br />It is <i>The Wind Through the Keyhole</i> within <i>The Skin-Man</i> within <i>The ka-tet's quest to the Dark Tower</i>.<br /><br />What reminded me also of Cloud Atlas was that the 1st 2 stories were cut in half by the middle (3rd) story and were continued at the end.<br />The core (Dark Tower) story is actually only 46 pages.<br />The Flashback to Roland's youth (Skin-Man) is 120 pages.<br />And the fairy tale (TWTTK) is 168 pages.<br /><br />The book starts just after they left the Green Palace (book 4) and a deadly blizzard (Starkblast) is coming and they need to find shelter. They eventually find it and while waiting for the storm to end Roland tells them a story from his youth.<br /><br />Just after his return from Mejis (book 4) Roland is sent to yet another quest. A skin-man similar to a werewolf but with multiple shifts/skins and much more dangerous, massacres a farm and Roland goes to investigate. A young boy is the sole survivor and Roland in order to calm him down tells him a bedtime story he remembers from his childhood;<br />this story is The Wind Through the Keyhole .<br />It contains fairies, swamps, dragons, wizards, swamp people, a man in black. It is an adventure of a young boy looking for a way to cure his mother's illness. <br /><br />I liked both stories (fairy tale &amp; flashback) and I'll say it again: I feel the core story is complete.<br />I need more stories from Roland's youth (Battle of Jericho Hill, his father's fate, his original ka-tet etc.)<br /><br />Many people ask if this is a stand alone book. Well if you read the fairy tale in the middle yes. If you also read the Skin-Man maybe, if you read the whole book a little less and in this case I would recommend to read the previous 4 books if you are more interested in the core story.<br />4 stars from me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2306172325921456392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2712657671" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2712657671" />
    <a title="SAM" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57392386-sam"><img alt="SAM" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556638019p2/57392386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2712657671?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="SAM" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SAM" href="/user/show/57392386-sam">SAM</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444731729" href="/book/show/17323860-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57392386-sam?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57392386-sam?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2712657671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12249608197667170979"><b>
  <i>"During the days after they left the Green Palace that wasn't Oz afterall - but which was now the tomb of the unpleasant fellow Rolland's ka-tet had known as the Tick-Tock Man - the boy Jake began to range farther and farther ahead of Roland, Eddie, and Susannah..."</i>
</b><br/><br/>I read the original Dark Tower books consecutively over a two month period in 2016 and was in awe that a fantasy series could be so mind-blowingly awesome. The series changed the way i perceived the fantasy genre and turned me int</span>
  <span id="freeText12249608197667170979" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"During the days after they left the Green Palace that wasn't Oz afterall - but which was now the tomb of the unpleasant fellow Rolland's ka-tet had known as the Tick-Tock Man - the boy Jake began to range farther and farther ahead of Roland, Eddie, and Susannah..."</i>
</b><br /><br />I read the original Dark Tower books consecutively over a two month period in 2016 and was in awe that a fantasy series could be so mind-blowingly awesome. The series changed the way i perceived the fantasy genre and turned me into a bookaholic!<br /><br />It’s taken a while to get around to The Wind Through the Key Hole mainly because ‘spin offs’ don’t really appeal to me. Most of the time they’re a novelty, cashing in on the success of the main original series. This isn’t quite at that level but compared to any one of the seven originals it’s worlds apart.<br /><br />We join the ka-tet just after Wizard and Glass on their journey to Calla Bryn Sturgis, the setting for Wolves of the Calla. There’s a badass storm approaching so cover is taken where Roland spins a tale from the old days. A younger Roland and companion Jamie are sent to investigate a series of murders by a possible ‘Skin Man’, who sounds like a more ungainly version of Mystique from X-Men. Midway through younger Roland spins another tale making this a story within a story within a story! The second tale, which he dubs The Wind Through the Keyhole, is almost half the book and isn’t as interesting as the Skin Man story. There’s a couple of references to the Man in Black, which put a nerdy smile on my face but for the most part the second story is way too long. I wanted more of the Skin Man tale, which is wrapped up and over way too soon.<br /><br />Unfortunately an average edition to the Dark Tower collection.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12249608197667170979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1357623709" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1357623709" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43881851-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557265090p2/43881851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1357623709?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781451658910" href="/book/show/15015023-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1357623709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4007575354453067365"><blockquote>
  <i>”A person's never too old for stories, Bill. Man and boy, girl and woman, never too old. We live for them.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>That would be <b>Roland Deschain</b> speaking, just before he tells a young Bill the story, <i>“The Wind Through the Keyhole”</i>, the very one his own mother had told him many a time before bed, some years earlier.<br/><br/>Slipped between Wizard & Glass and Wolves of the Calla, the Dark Tower novel 4.5 didn't feel like a transition between those two bigger books at the time, but of course it had come later. </span>
  <span id="freeText4007575354453067365" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>”A person's never too old for stories, Bill. Man and boy, girl and woman, never too old. We live for them.”</i>
</blockquote><br />That would be <b>Roland Deschain</b> speaking, just before he tells a young Bill the story, <i>“The Wind Through the Keyhole”</i>, the very one his own mother had told him many a time before bed, some years earlier.<br /><br />Slipped between Wizard &amp; Glass and Wolves of the Calla, the Dark Tower novel 4.5 didn't feel like a transition between those two bigger books at the time, but of course it had come later. Like most everyone else, I hadn't been inside the Gunslinger’s world (or worlds) with Roland for nearly ten a decade. Still, I adored this little book at the time, and I think the “going back” was a big part of the why, just as it is now with each book I return to. The idea of the Starkblast seized me, in a similar way it does Roland and the others. As they batten the hatches and hunker down to wait out the storm, they listen to the second story Roland would tell over the span of two books. Once again, it is the days of the young Roland they hear about, but which then evolves into another story wrapped inside of the first. The second story is where this book gets it's title “The Wind Through the Keyhole”. For the reader then, this book is three stories in one. Each grasp me, <i>or you</i>, in their own way. One is a bookends, another is an intro leading back to the past, and the third is the heart. It's the reason for the telling, but the way it's told and who about is why I like it. The Starkblast becomes memory's trigger for both the elder and younger Roland here. As it rolls over our Ka-tet in hiding, so will it do within that middle story where we meet a young boy named Tim. He's a boy who would face any fear out of love for his mother, and the storm is not the only fear he will face. A child against the odds is a story King tells very well, and don't we know it.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>”And so it happened, once upon a bye, long before your grandfather's grandfather was born.”</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="4007575354453067365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_274571817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274571817" />
    <a title="T.J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5460996-t-j"><img alt="T.J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546275981p2/5460996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274571817?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="T.J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="T.J." href="/user/show/5460996-t-j">T.J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274571817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7007014374994741477">A wonderful entry into the Dark Tower series that King supposedly completed in 2004. Think of this as DT 4.5, after Glass and before Wolves. We don't spend much time with the Ka-tet, as Roland tells them a story of his past while they take shelter from a storm (a "starkblast"--great imagery behind that name). As Roland tells the tale of hunting a shifter in a small town, King then takes it further and tells a story WITHIN the story, that of a boy who must attempt to save his mother's life. It's </span>
  <span id="freeText7007014374994741477" style="display:none">A wonderful entry into the Dark Tower series that King supposedly completed in 2004. Think of this as DT 4.5, after Glass and before Wolves. We don't spend much time with the Ka-tet, as Roland tells them a story of his past while they take shelter from a storm (a "starkblast"--great imagery behind that name). As Roland tells the tale of hunting a shifter in a small town, King then takes it further and tells a story WITHIN the story, that of a boy who must attempt to save his mother's life. It's this middle story that takes up the bulk of the book and it too was just gorgeously written. A great addition to the Dark Tower series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7007014374994741477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2111382506" />
    <a title="Justin Brendel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10609503-justin-brendel"><img alt="Justin Brendel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566220262p2/10609503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2111382506?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin Brendel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin Brendel" href="/user/show/10609503-justin-brendel">Justin Brendel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781501166228" href="/book/show/32333000-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2111382506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16068961621842596024">The story within a story concept is ok, but it doesn't really progress our ka-tet to the Dark Tower. I do love The Wind Through The Keyhole story within this book. The Skin Man, not so much. I feel these were story ideas King had but couldn't create a final product, so this book became essentially three short stories nested within each other. On to the calla!</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_326722997" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326722997" />
    <a title="unknown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2863914-unknown"><img alt="unknown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579703867p2/2863914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/326722997?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="unknown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="unknown" href="/user/show/2863914-unknown">unknown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781451658903" href="/book/show/12106746-the-wind-through-the-keyhole">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=dark-tower-y">dark-tower-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=ride-em-cowboy">ride-em-cowboy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326722997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1418967824910487029">I have read a few negative reviews of this book that make <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322084015' rel='nofollow noopener'>excellent</a> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163302962' rel='nofollow noopener'>points</a> about why this is a disappointing addition to the Dark Tower canon. I can't really disagree with them. And yet I enjoyed this story. The difference, I think, lies more with my expectations than the execution.<br/><br/>My favorite part of the Dark Tower is the world King slowly assembled over the course of the series, and the way he eventually tied it in to a dozen or so of his other novels, creating a vast meta-fictional landscape.</span>
  <span id="freeText1418967824910487029" style="display:none">I have read a few negative reviews of this book that make <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322084015" rel="nofollow noopener">excellent</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163302962" rel="nofollow noopener">points</a> about why this is a disappointing addition to the Dark Tower canon. I can't really disagree with them. And yet I enjoyed this story. The difference, I think, lies more with my expectations than the execution.<br /><br />My favorite part of the Dark Tower is the world King slowly assembled over the course of the series, and the way he eventually tied it in to a dozen or so of his other novels, creating a vast meta-fictional landscape. In fact, I'd go so far as to say that I care more about the world than the characters -- I care about the characters quite a lot. But the parts I really like reading are the weird little details of this world that has moved on: rusting heaps of leftover technology, unfamiliar brands of soda, giant bear robots, insane sentient trains. That stuff.<br /><br />I went into The Wind Through the Keyhole <i>knowing</i> it was going to be a filler novel. I read that King believed it could stand alone, so I was pretty sure it wasn't going to offer up much detail on the ka-tet's between-book adventures. And in fact, I read the main series so long ago I... kind of forgot there was any discontinuity there (me and Stephen King both, I guess).<br /><br />So my wishlist for this book included one item, which was any Dark Tower lore, but I wasn't expecting it, because I knew it was some kind of story-within-a-story fairytale thing. And then, I got some! Because within these nested tales are more details on the Guardians of the Beam and North Central Positronics, and there's even one of those sympathetic artificial intelligences that I find so endearing (even when they are crazy and murderous -- PATRICIA + BLAINE 4-EVER!). This time, I'm feeling pathos for an ancient GPS*.<br /><br /><i>* Never mind that it doesn't make much sense that this fairytale, ostensibly from an old book that Roland's mother used to read to him, would include incredibly specific details about the Crimson King-esque shenanigans going on throughout the series. More oblique Charlie the Choo-Choo-style nods would present the information in a far more internally consistent manner. But then again, we wouldn't have any scenes with your friendly neighborhood sentient GPS, so...</i><br /><br />Yeah, ok, so the rest of the book isn't the best. The framing sections with Roland, Eddie, Jake, et al. are cursory at best, and almost feel like fan-fiction (though to be totally honest, I <i>kind of</i> feel that way about everything in the series after the knock on the gates of Oz, especially the parts of book 5 with the Harry Potter exploding snitches and the Doctors Doom with lightsabers), but it's still fun to peek in on those characters again while they are all still, you know, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[alive <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />The second-level framing device (stick with me), featuring Young Roland, pleased me more than I expected, considering I kind of hated the flashback-heavy fourth book in the series. It helped that it was short, action-packed, and not a story of angsty teen love. I still have no idea what is up with the fall of Gilead and the Battle of Jericho Hill and all that jazz though. I guess I have to read the comics for that.<br /><br />So, yeah. Context. If you go into this one expecting an honest-to-Gan Dark Tower novel, you'll be bummed, because it really isn't one. It kind of seems like it took King about a week to write, and he just had fun messing around with it (which doesn't bode well for his sequel to The Shining). If you are a reader who has spent $25 on the hardcover and invested a chunk of time reading it, that may not be enough for you. If you are me, and borrowed your brother's audiobook copy and listened to it at 3x speed on your phone, maybe it will be. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1418967824910487029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wucINegG8C/7Jh59iqx0lC+oyrDgRPlE8lIn0C6kPb6uQq3JWne+WKK+rrpM+FfocdCNIHufHVxP8vKqN5Gt3A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7x66/iOX2tZ1V0f7EraGZPAseqbnwoxGE/lEn7r7By6Dux8CkeaUoSzP9zzU4qUYrlQ9NnwZaF6uWZHlo86XTA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
750,402
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2248708544883609951">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText2248708544883609951" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2248708544883609951" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
